S\u1ef1 \u0110a D\u1ea1ng H\u00f3a Th\u1ecb Tr\u01b0\u1eddng:\n\n- Ngo\u00e0i Bitcoin, th\u1ecb tr\u01b0\u1eddng crypto \u0111\u00e3 ph\u00e1t tri\u1ec3n v\u1edbi s\u1ef1 xu\u1ea5t hi\u1ec7n c\u1ee7a h\u00e0ng ng\u00e0n \u0111\u1ed3ng ti\u1ec1n \u0111i\u1ec7n t\u1eed kh\u00e1c nhau, bao g\u1ed3m Ethereum, Ripple, Litecoin v\u00e0 nhi\u1ec1u altcoin kh\u00e1c.\n\n- S\u1ef1 \u0111a d\u1ea1ng n\u00e0y \u0111\u00e3 t\u1ea1o ra m\u1ed9t th\u1ecb tr\u01b0\u1eddng phong ph\u00fa v\u00e0 \u0111a d\u1ea1ng, cho ph\u00e9p ng\u01b0\u1eddi d\u00f9ng l\u1ef1a ch\u1ecdn theo nhu c\u1ea7u c\u1ee7a h\u1ecd.\n\n\ud83d\udd39II. Ch\u00eca kh\u00f3a ri\u00eang t\u01b0 l\u00e0 th\u1ee9 duy nh\u1ea5t cho ph\u00e9p b\u1ea1n truy c\u1eadp v\u00e0 ki\u1ec3m so\u00e1t t\u00e0i s\u1ea3n c\u1ee7a m\u00ecnh.\nT\u1ea1i Sao V\u00ed L\u1ea1nh \u0110\u01b0\u1ee3c Coi L\u00e0 An To\u00e0n?\nV\u00ed l\u1ea1nh \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c xem l\u00e0 an to\u00e0n v\u00ec n\u00f3 kh\u00f4ng k\u1ebft n\u1ed1i tr\u1ef1c ti\u1ebfp v\u1edbi internet. \u0110i\u1ec1u n\u00e0y c\u00f3 ngh\u0129a l\u00e0 hacker kh\u00f4ng th\u1ec3 truy c\u1eadp v\u00e0o v\u00ed c\u1ee7a b\u1ea1n t\u1eeb xa. \u0110i\u1ec1u n\u00e0y \u0111\u00e3 \u0111\u1ed5i m\u1edbi c\u00e1ch l\u01b0u tr\u1eef v\u00e0 b\u1ea3o v\u1ec7 ti\u1ec1n \u0111i\u1ec7n t\u1eed so v\u1edbi v\u00ed tr\u1ef1c tuy\u1ebfn, n\u01a1i t\u00e0i s\u1ea3n c\u1ee7a b\u1ea1n c\u00f3 th\u1ec3 b\u1ecb \u0111e d\u1ecda b\u1edfi c\u00e1c cu\u1ed9c t\u1ea5n c\u00f4ng tr\u1ef1c tuy\u1ebfn.\nTuy Nhi\u00ean, V\u1eabn Y\u00eau C\u1ea7u S\u1ef1 Th\u1eadn Tr\u1ecdng C\u1ee7a B\u1ea1n:\n\ud83d\udc49R\u1ee7i Ro T\u1eeb Vi\u1ec7c M\u1ea5t Ch\u00eca Kh\u00f3a: \n\u0110\u1ec3 tr\u00e1nh vi\u1ec7c m\u1ea5t v\u00ed l\u1ea1nh, ng\u01b0\u1eddi d\u00f9ng th\u01b0\u1eddng l\u01b0u tr\u1eef ch\u00eca kh\u00f3a ri\u00eang t\u01b0 ho\u1eb7c passphrase (\u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c s\u1eed d\u1ee5ng \u0111\u1ec3 kh\u00f4i ph\u1ee5c) t\u1ea1i m\u1ed9t n\u01a1i kh\u00e1c, ch\u1eb3ng h\u1ea1n nh\u01b0 in tr\u00ean gi\u1ea5y, l\u01b0u tr\u00ean Google Drive, Gmail ho\u1eb7c m\u00e1y t\u00ednh c\u1ee7a h\u1ecd. Let's talk about common questions from creators when we do a payout.\n\nThe two biggest questions I get are:\n\n(1) I didn't get a payment\n(2) My payment was low\n\nOn (1), there is a minimum payout threshold of $10. If you don't meet the threshold, you aren't paid during that payout. You do of course keep accumulating earnings until you reach the threshold, until $10 is reached.\n\nThere are many practical reasons for this. The most important reason is fees associated with the transfer, which would potentially eat into a creator's earnings.\n\nOn (2), I've looked into dozens of cases about low payouts, especially for high follower / high impression accounts. Many creators assume that ads CPM x impression = their payout, but unfortunately it's not that simple. Although high impressions are of course correlated with a larger payout, the demographic of your audience and how they engage is also a very important factor.\n\nMajor factors that explain why such an account may receive a lower payout than expected include:\n\n1. Ads are shown, but the audience is not Verified. Revenue is only earned for ads shown to Verified users. This is one of many ways we mitigate attempts to manipulate the program.\n\n2. Ads are shown, but the ad spend on ads shown to the creator's demographic is low. It's a revenue share program - creators earn a % of what X earns. Ads generate more revenue in different markets and to different audiences.\n\n3. Some of the creator's content may not be suitable for ads. If we can't show ads on some of your posts, that affects your revenue.\n\n4. Content is compelling to scroll by in the timeline, but not compelling to reply to. {"id": 1713456223310512175, "id_str": "1713456223310512175", "url": "https://twitter.com/LTaylor22851/status/1713456223310512175", "date": "2023-10-15 07:26:12+00:00", "user": {"id": 1706197804576899072, "id_str": "1706197804576899072", "url": "https://twitter.com/LTaylor22851", "username": "LTaylor22851", "displayname": "Lucinda Taylor", "rawDescription": "", "created": "2023-09-25 06:44:11+00:00", "followersCount": 1151, "friendsCount": 191, "statusesCount": 61, "favouritesCount": 21, "listedCount": 0, "mediaCount": 12, "location": "", "profileImageUrl": "https://pbs.twimg.com/profile_images/1706403033268264961/LLoqGs8l_normal.jpg", "profileBannerUrl": null, "protected": null, "verified": false, "blue": true, "blueType": null, "descriptionLinks": [], "_type": "snscrape.modules.twitter.User"}, "lang": "en", "rawContent": "Intents (1) have recently gained prominence as a solution to the challenges encountered by users in the current Web3 paradigm. Today, while millions of users utilize blockchains to conduct transactions, there\u2019s a noticeable gap; among the total of 5.19B internet users (2) , less than 100M possess blockchain wallets (3) , the primary gateways to decentralized applications (\u201cdApps\u201d). What's hindering Web3 from broader adoption? For starters, engaging with current Web3 systems can be a complex and time-consuming task, especially for those not well-versed with such technologies. These steep learning curves significantly heighten the entry barriers, deterring a large cohort of potential users from stepping into the ecosystem. To interact with blockchains, users are required to navigate fragmented infrastructures to piece together an execution route; this includes creating and signing transactions in a specific format, potentially using multiple applications and blockchains, and explicitly providing all information to reach a desired outcome. Such complexity often leads to a sub-optimal user experience (\u201cUX\u201d), is prone to errors, and paves the way for potential exploitation of MEV by more sophisticated actors.\nAs a result, intents emerged as a solution to overcome these challenges, with the aim of simplifying Web3 interactions for users. But what exactly are intents? Intents are signed messages that enable users to express what they want to achieve on-chain, while third-party actors, known as solvers, handle the technical details to make it happen. At their core, intents comprise a set of declarative constraints; users delegate transaction creation to solvers, who choose the best computational path on their behalf, all while retaining full control over their assets. In layman's terms, intents allow users to focus on their end goals - the \u2018what\u2019 - without being bogged down by the specific steps - the \u2018how\u2019 - to realize those goals. Intent-centric solutions can be thought of as order flow abstraction. They pave the way for dApps to mirror the UX of conventional applications. Users are no longer burdened by the complexities associated with blockchain interactions; instead, these are passed onto solvers. This is particularly beneficial as the industry progresses toward a multi-Layer-2 (\u201cL2\u201d), multichain landscape. While Ethereum's rollup-centric roadmap solves for scalability, it introduces asynchronous states across a multitude of chains, in other words, it adds complexity to how information is processed and managed among these chains. This compromise adds challenges for users attempting to navigate this space. With intents, a substantial portion of the complexities associated with cross-chain liquidity, chain swapping, bridge selection and more are delegated to these backend solvers. Ultimately, intents are poised to transform the Web3 experience, transitioning it from a manual, step-by-step process to a more intuitive, outcome-focused approach. They offer the prospect of smoother transactions, faster execution, and improved UX.#Binance\ud83d\udcf7 #Crypto #Bnb\ud83d\udcf7 #Bitcoin\ud83d\udcf7", "replyCount": 19, "retweetCount": 0, "likeCount": 10, "quoteCount": 0, "conversationId": 1713456223310512175, "hashtags": [], "cashtags": [], "mentionedUsers": [], "links": [], "viewCount": 342, "retweetedTweet": null, "quotedTweet": null, "place": null, "coordinates": null, "inReplyToTweetId": null, "inReplyToUser": null, "source": "<a href=\"https://mobile.twitter.com\" rel=\"nofollow\">Twitter Web App</a>", "sourceUrl": "https://mobile.twitter.com", "sourceLabel": "Twitter Web App", "media": {"photos": [{"url": "https://pbs.twimg.com/media/F8drWT5a0AAdZn1.png"}], "videos": [], "animated": []}, "_type": "snscrape.modules.twitter.Tweet"}
